## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x and time t. In classical mechanics, the acceleration is determined by the restoring force, which for nonlinear oscillators includes terms beyond the linear Hooke's law (e.g., cubic nonlinearities like Duffing oscillator, damping terms, and possible external driving forces).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven, undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * dv_dt_proxy (damping requires velocity, but acceleration-position relation)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodically driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (driven simple harmonic oscillator)
- Driven oscillator with damping proxy: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (general driven Duffing)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Van der Pol-like: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * x (self-excited oscillation structure, using x as proxy)
- Sinusoidal restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum-like nonlinearity)
- Driven with nonlinear restoring: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven pendulum)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells, characteristic of Duffing-type oscillators
- Periodic driving terms cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) → external forcing in driven oscillator systems
- Sign of cubic coefficient determines hardening (negative with negative linear) vs softening spring behavior
- Time-dependent coefficients multiplying x → parametric excitation or modulated stiffness
- Sinusoidal function of position sin(c*x) → large-amplitude pendulum dynamics with geometric nonlinearity
- Mixed even and odd powers of x → asymmetric potential (broken symmetry in restoring force)
- Product of trigonometric function of t with polynomial in x → parametrically driven nonlinear oscillator
- Acceleration depending only on x (no explicit t) → autonomous conservative or dissipative system

- **Candidate 5**: rational in x + sin(t). Simplifies to `(c0 + c4/(c2*x²+1))·x + c3·sin(t)`. This gives `a·x + b·x/(c·x²+1) + d·sin(t)`. The term `x/(x²+c)` is NOT equivalent to `x·exp(-|x|)`. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 11**: Simplifies to `c0*x/(c1*x²+1) + c2*x + c3*x³ + c4*sin(t)`. Polynomial + rational, no exp(-|x|). [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 16**: Simplifies to `c0*sin(t) + c2*x/(c1+x²) + c3*x + c4`. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 18**: `c0*x + c2*sin(t) + c3*x/(c1+x²)`. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 35**: `c0*x³ + c2*x/(c1+x²) + c3*sin(t)`. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 42**: `c0*x⁵ + c2*x/(c1+x²) + c3*sin(t)`. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 49**: `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*sin(t) + c3*x⁵`. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 48**: `c0*cos(c1*t) + c2*sin(t) + c3*x⁵ + c4*x³ + c5*x`. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 10**: Simplifies to `c0*c2*x³ + c0*x + c3*x/(c1+x²) + c4*sin(t)`. [NO MATCH]

**Candidates with sin(c·x) terms:**
`sin(c·x)` is NOT equivalent to `x·exp(-|x|)` — these are linearly independent functions.

- **Candidates 1, 3, 6, 7, 8, 15, 19, 20, 24, 26, 27, 28, 29, 37, 39, 40, 43, 44, 45, 46**: All contain `sin(c·x)` as a basis function but no `exp(-|x|)`. Since `sin(c·x)` cannot equal `x·exp(-|x|)`, these are [NO MATCH].

**Candidates with exp(c·x²):**
`exp(c·x²)` with c<0 gives a Gaussian, NOT `exp(-|x|)`. These are fundamentally different functions. [NO MATCH] for: 9, 12, 13, 14, 20, 21, 22, 23, 25, 30, 31, 34, 36, 41, 47, 50, 51, 52, 53, 54, 55, 56, 57, 58.

**Candidate 30**: `c0 + c1*x + c2*sin(t) + c3*x*log(c4*x²+1)`. `x·log(c·x²+1)` ≠ `x·exp(-|x|)`. [NO MATCH]

**Remaining candidates** (17, 32, 33, 38): These are polynomial/rational + trig in t only. [NO MATCH]

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can produce the `x·exp(-|x|)` basis function present in the GT.
